# LaCroix Board Co. &ndash; wood and CF deck + segmented flex carbon fiber enclosure &ndash; GROUP BUY \[COMPLETED\]

### Replies: 1505 Views: 57683

## \#1 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-03-14T02:22:39.429Z Reads: 1734

```
![25|690x459](upload://jnraEiznn0jmoVFSax9oFpYOjE8.jpg)

Hey Everyone,

TLDR; flexible AT canadian maple/CF board with CF enclosure for 72 single stacked 18650 cells. On sale. Now. 

My brother (@pat_arch) and I are launching the Lacroix Board Co. (www.lacroixboards.com) to fill a gap in the market ; high speed, long range, pneu-only, flexible non-mountain board.

We built a 10s4p (30Q) and a 12s4p (30Q) trampa urban carver last summer and got hooked. After 3000km of riding, there were some things we liked and some we didn't (none related to @Kaly 's parts though!). We liked the pneumatics (how they are forgiving at high speed, on uneven, cracked and pot-holed roads as well as versatile for gravel, grass and sand) and we also really appreciated the flex of the board - with the caveat that the trampa deck derives from land kite and mountain boards which need to absorb jumps (probably where the hard-to-get-used-to arch comes from). Anyways, e-boards are not meant to leave the ground so we found the deck to be somewhat misadapted. Plus it has no concave, and we've had various issues with trampa trucks and wheels etc etc etc. 

Long story short we decided last September to build a new e-board from the ground up using our experience in various board sports and the knowledge we had acquired in e-boards.

Having personally been riding snowboards, surfboards and kite-surfs for over 20 years, we also used that experience to build a board that would feel like the best deep powder run. Like surfing at NazarÃ©. Like kiting in 30 knot winds. We wanted to create a board that would feel so good you'd have goosebumps and nervous giggles while riding it. A board that is fast and that commands respect. And as long as you do, will provide endless daily shots of endorphined adrenaline (we just made that up but fairly sure it's a thing).

Here is our long list of engineering and design constraints;

* Build the GT3 RS of e-boards. High speed. Long range. No compromise.
* Flexible Canadian Maple deck.
* Flexible carbon fiber enclosure (non conductive).
* Must hold at least 60 single stacked 18650 cells.

We designed the deck and enclosure with a big wave surfboard and longboard engineer. The board and enclosure were conceived together. The flex, the look, the feel, all were engineered and designed by considering both board and enclosure, as one.

Fast forward a couple months and we're thrilled to present you the Lacroix DSS60. The Dynamics and Speed Study (we sell it with 60 cells) is unique. The decks are handmade, one at the time. The carbon fiber enclosures are crafted in a motorsports atelier.

The board feels amazing. It rides like nothing else.

So why we here? This site is full of selfless people always willing to help and relentless about filtering the BS (which makes its content so valuable). As a way of thanking you for the knowledge, crazy experiments and general badassery, my brother and I want to offer you the possibility of purchasing our deck and enclosure at a low price to build it up the way you want and give us your feedback. All boards will be identified as "prototipo" as seen in the pics.

This is a one time offer for the members on this site only. This is our very small way of giving back to the community - we know the "prototipo" will make you smile. A lot.

**PRICE**; 

USD$375 + shipping. Payment must be made through the website (https://www.lacroixboards.com/product-page/board-carbon-fiber-enclosure-prototipo). 

EDIT; we had a coupon code at first but we had some feedback the coupon code was not working in some countries. So we now provide the discount directly on the website, no coupon code needed. 

**INCLUDED**;

* Hand made flexible board, crafted from a proprietary combination of Canadian maple wood, thin layers of fibers, topped with a beautiful carbon fiber layer to insure maximum flexibility and durability.  
* Pre-installed German-made inserts and closed-cell recessed foam strip for water resistance.
* Carbon fiber and fiberglass enclosure with pre-drilled holes.
* Stainless steel screws, countersunk aluminum washers and nylon washers.
* EDIT; Clear grip tape 

**EXCLUDED**;

* Hole(s) in the enclosure for the motor wires. You can place those wherever you feel like. If this feels too much for you... We have no clue how you got to reading this far on a DIY forum ;)

**DIMENSIONS & WEIGHT**

Deck;
* Deck length (with tabs): 34.5in / 876mm
* Deck length (without tabs): 27in / 686mm
* Deck width: 10.75in / 273mm
* EDIT ; Tabs angle ; 30 degrees
* EDIT; Deck weight ; 4.4 lbs including seal, inserts and screws (w/o griptape).

Enclosure specs:
* Cell compartments: 3in x 9.25in / 76mm x 235mm EDIT; when building your batterypack, you should keep your overall thickness below 25mm.
* VESC compartment (this is where 12 extra cells fit if you get creative) 5.25in x 9.25 / 133mmx235mm, minus the rounded corners
* EDIT; enclosure weight ; 1.1 lbs.

EDIT; **total weight** (deck + enclosure + hardware w/o griptape) ; 5.5 lbs

**FITS**;

* 60 cells (18650) comfortably (tested and running)
* 72 cells (18650) snug (only fit tested)
* 50 cells (21700) comfortably (only fit tested)
* 60 cells (21700) snug (only fit tested)
* MBS and Trampa trucks - 11 inch to 15.5 inch have been tested with no wheel-bite or heel-bite. If using 11 inch trucks, 7 inch tires are recommended. 8 inch tires might rub depending on tire model). The board is pre-drilled for MBS trucks. If you use Trampa trucks, youâ€™ll need to drill holes for the damper screw (the ones that compress the springs and dampas). 

**EST. SHIP DATE**; mid to end of may 2018, just in time for the summer!

TIMELINE; the discount price will be valid only until the end of the month of March, **i.e. it will expire on March 31st 2018 at 23h59pm**. After that date, decks and enclosures will be available at the regular price of USD$699 + shipping.

Finally, after doing some research on the perfect backpack to transport our boards, we partnered with Osprey - an amazing company that only does one thing, backpacks. If you are looking for a small (22 litres) backpack that can easily and comfortably carry a 20lbs+ board, check it out here; https://www.lacroixboards.com/product-page/osprey-x-lacroix-22l-board-backpack. It has pockets on the waist belt for the remote, an integrated helmet net, a soft pouch for your sunglasses. It fits a laptop and it carries an e-board like it ain't no thang. Oh, and it also doubles as a backcountry ski and snowboard bag. 2 for 1 baby. The backpacks are available now (in blue) and ship right away. They come branded with the LaCroix logo, as seen in the pics. 

The shipping quote you get from the website is an estimate - although we hope not to, we might need to revert back with the actual shipping price and ask you to cover the difference if the actual shipping is higher. Inversely, if itâ€™s lower, weâ€™ll refund the difference.

PS; the motormounts on the DSS60 are the work of art of @Yann with the X-Design inspired by @Riako. Merci encore Yann, superbe travail!

PPS; special craft-beer-filled thanks to @JohnnyMeduse and @Blasto for teaching us a million things and helping us on this amazing journey. You guys rock. Hard.

PPPS; we are looking for an app maker for our board. If you're interested, DM dawg.

PPPPS (this is getting out of hand); the price of 7 inch and 8 inch pneumatics is insane for some reason (350%+ markups). So we decided to do something about it. We currently are selling some 7 inch tires (incl. tubes) at reasonable prices (USD$35 for 4 tires and tubes + shipping) so people can ride freely and treat them for what they are, ie consumables. 

PPPPPS (fuck it, we're both here aren't we!); sorry if much of this info seems to be repeated on the website. We actually drafted this post first and then pick and choosed a bunch of stuff from here for the website - which we launched yesterday.

Cheers, 

Alex & Pat

## \#30 Posted by: pat_arch Posted at: 2018-03-14T17:11:21.877Z Reads: 651

```
Thanks man!

Our enclosures are made in a motorsports atelier that makes race cars. We managed to get them excited about our project and agreed to work with us. As @Deckoz mentionned, we indeed use prepreg twill carbon fiber and and obtain the smooth finish with a combination of vacuum bagging and autoclaving techniques.
```

## \#46 Posted by: mmaner Posted at: 2018-03-15T12:13:11.733Z Reads: 548

```
The MBS trucks use a plastic baseplate, but the hangers them selves are far stronger.  MBS trucks have been around for years with far less failures and design flaws (vibration cracks, etc). 

Every trampa I've ever ridden (admittedly not many) the hangers flex, one of the things that turns me off of them. 

I'm all for innovation, hell I wouldn't be building esk8s if I wasn't, but sometimes the available solution is the best solution until new technology displaces the old solution. There's no new tech in mountainboard trucks.
```

## \#52 Posted by: banjaxxed Posted at: 2018-03-15T13:07:14.912Z Reads: 559

```
I can't get over a structural component like that being made out of plastic, it's true unless you want to make something for really cheap and load up on the price. Not sure what plastic but let's just say nylon, let's have a look at some figures
https://www.makeitfrom.com/compare/6061-O-Aluminum/Polyamide-PA-Nylon-6-10-610

In essence there will be a whole lot of force being applied from the hanger->kingpin->small circular plastic ring on each side of the baseplate, I drew the springs in that MBS were too cheap to put in, sorry I mean that their PU dampers are so much more superior to anyone elses's that they don't need springs
![image|640x400](upload://hDdTXhxrKlLUPy6MMz9NfteyS2d.jpg)

The MBS baseplate is much better at being elongated before breaking, that about it really the aluminium which incidentally is forged increasing strength over cast

Anyway enough with the bashing, MBS has it's place for quasi-rough or street riding, certainly they are lighter given plastic, no springs & maybe a bit cheaper (if you live in the USA).

I have TWO farking iphones, a 5 and a 6, the 5 was a present the 6 is for work, not really bothered I was thinking a nice android when it comes time but they both do their job well and it's important to be able to trouser the phone unlike the behemoths that came out in the last few years.

I love you man, chill

@trampa thanks, do you have the tracking number?

Ps. One last fanboy comment, the whisper on the hanger crack, pictured here
![image|666x500](upload://hIIBoyJSnYUeKD5nmFi0KaZ00qP.jpg)

was determined to be contributed heavily by the use of solid MBS wheels, in saying that I'd say the solid Infinity would not have gone that way if using a solid wheel was important with offroad hangers, god know why you'd want to.

## \#55 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-03-15T14:16:50.152Z Reads: 541

```
Guys, while we certainly appreciate the passion, we do not intend on entertaining a Trampa vs MBS war here.

Pat and I tested both setups thoroughly (MBS and Trampa) for what we want our board to be, a high speed, long range, pneu-only, flexible non-mountain board.

Weâ€™ve found the MBS Matrix2 trucks to be overall much better for our needs, ie lighter, very
maneuverable at low speeds (no more picking up the board to point it in a different direction because the turning radius is much better) and no speed wobble at high speeds (without changing any setup). As briefly discussed, I broke a baseplate on my Vertigo truck and Pat bent a hanger on his. Can that happen on MBS? If the MBS had a hairline crack like my Trampa did, then yes, most probably. Nothing is indestructible. 

This said, in this Trampa vs MBS argument, the crux of the matter generally doesn't revolve around the aluminum portions of the trucks. Nor the fact that the Matrix2 completely deleted the spring (which imo is the real revolution behind this truck). The argument revolves around the composite baseplate of the Matrix2. 

Selling boards that are fast, we have a responsability towards our clients to provide a safe product (At the moment, Trampa doesn't sell boards that include battery-packs. There is a reason for that. The liability risks are real. For any manufacturer). And we take that very seriously. So here's the fact around this liability (which has many facets); we have not been been shown any actionable data demonstrating that the composite top plate of the Matrix2 is weaker than an aluminum plate. No evidence that would show a pattern of weakness enabling us to conclude that the documented cases of breakage are anything else than outliers. To conclude it's generally _weaker_ (and hence potentially dangerous), there would need to be patterns of behavior under similar conditions. We have been shown none. 

So from this situation, we conluded that, at worst, both Trampa and MBS are equal. This said, the ride feel and flexibility, the weight savings - namely by the fact they deleted 2 springs on the Matrix2 - , coupled with the great customer service we had from the guys at MBS made us lean in that direction. 

Again, we're not here to preach or bash anyone, I'm just sharing my personal experience. You may have had a different experience with the company and the products than we have had. 

I will conclude with this; if you've never actually tried a Matrix2 truck and have the opportunity to try one (on a friend's board etc), you should. It feels very different than a spring and egg truck. And after that, _if you still prefer the spring and egg Trampa_, that's more than ok. Not everybody likes Porsches.

As Pat said, we will more than happily accommodate you guys by drilling the right
holes for the build you want - Trampa trucks included. Because at the end of the day, we all just want the same thing. To go out and shred. 

Now if some moderator would be so kind as to flip all this side discussion to another thread, that would be much appreciated.

Cheers, 
A
```

---
## \#56 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-03-15T14:52:09.955Z Reads: 492

```
Thanks @banjaxxed! Clearly had my acronyms crossed. In terms of group buys, as was said, the only place where you would be saving is potentially on shipping. Although keep in mind we only charge _actual_ shipping price (you're refunded if our estimate was too high and you pay a bit more if it was too low). So if we ship one big box of products to ireland, then you have a second shipping price to get the products to your door. I might be wrong, but I don't think the hassle would be worth it. You'd _maybe_ be saving a couple of bucks and that remains to be seen. To me, GB are more pertinent when you can get a discount on the product by buying bullk. Here, we are already offering you the steepest discount we can. We basically consider you guys as a huge group buy, with the caveat that we go through the trouble of shipping to all of you individually, not a single address.
```

## \#62 Posted by: benjammin Posted at: 2018-03-15T17:41:32.338Z Reads: 491

```

---
## \#63 Posted by: pat_arch Posted at: 2018-03-15T17:54:50.669Z Reads: 508

```
The board has a front/back arch and a heel/toe concave which is more pronounced in the middle.

So in order to have the same workable space for the batteries in the middle of the deck, the enclosure appears to be thicker when looking at it from the side but it does in fact have the same 25mm clearance in the middle.

![cut deck|690x228](upload://6fLksGVY3lSUWFS7fmIsCb6k8yj.jpg)
```

## \#67 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-03-15T18:49:02.206Z Reads: 499

```
also, note the board wasn't designed for jumping. The flex was engineered for carving, not for absorbing jumps (although going on and off curbs is certainly not a problem, besides maybe scratching the motormount). Also, I'd recommend trying the board before installing bindings. It's much wider than conventional boards and if you use the Matrix2, you'll find your lean angle will surprise you. Anyhow, maybe you'll prefer bindings, I'm just saying you should try the board without for at least a couple of days before making the call. 
Cheers, 
A
```

Just to add to this and to give you guys a very rough idea, when putting my whole 185lbs body on my heel or my toes (to flex the Matrix II Pro truck on 7 inch tires) to simulate a deep carve, I have approx 1 or 1.5inch of space between the enclosure and the ground. ## \#133 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-03-22T13:15:54.260Z Reads: 374

```
Ahhhhhhhh, didn't know that detail. So the unikboards riser might be misadapted, I'm not sure. Anyhow, the point is a small riser would be needed for 5inch tires and possibly for 6 inch tires as well depending on how aggressively you flex the board when carving and what type of terrain you ride (on a bumpy surface we would recommend a slightly higher ride height - the enclosure on 5 inch and 6 inch tires might rub the ground during a deep carve over some bump in the asphalt).
```

---

## \#238 Posted by: Ovi Posted at: 2018-05-13T18:23:22.055Z Reads: 368

```
[quote="Sender, post:236, topic:49051"]
Surfrodz RKP
[/quote]


This is just my humble two cents, take it, roll it and do what you seem fit with my opinion, but seriously the "stock" setup is so awesome! My two cents might not be worth its full weight because it is my first esk8 BUT I can tell you this much - I've been pushing an analog Loaded Dervish on Paris trucks, Kegels and ceramic bearings with cones for bushings both top and bottom with almost no pressure on them for a few years now. If there's one thing I was afraid to miss from that setup it was its carving ability. And boy does the LaCroix carve! I wouldn't change a thing, I'm leaning on it in corners like in a Michael Jackson videoclip and at the same time it is soooo stable - 35-38 km/h doesn't give you the spooks because of how wide this thing is. 

As for the wheels, yes @psychotiller has some epic epic wheels and I myself reached out to @Arch and @pat_arch right after I ordered it to ask if I could get the aluminium MBS wheels instead. I'm very happy I didn't. The board looks even better in person, and the whole purist stealth look fits it beautifully. It's bold, it's powerful but it doesn't scream that when you look at it. It sits there elegantly until you press the throttle and then it becomes the beast they say. 

Again, please forgive my excitement and like I said I can only speak about this board compared to the Trampa they lent me for a week before and for my Dervish. I haven't tried any other trucks than the ones on the DSS60 / Trampa / Paris, maybe Surfrodz are as nice, but as it is now, the stock setup feels anything but generic, I don't see how anybody who tries it out could not fall in love with it.

Cheers everyone!
```

## \#264 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-05-16T16:41:57.578Z Reads: 378

```
Guys, to save you some time and order this in advance. Making holes in carbon fiber is much easier with a step drill. For the power button for example, if you need to make a 16mm hole, you'll have a hard time doing it with a 16mm bit. Better to use something like this. 

https://www.amazon.ca/Bestgle-Speed-Steel-Titanium-Quick-change/dp/B06XNMGV9R/ref=sr_1_4?ie=UTF8&qid=1526488823&sr=8-4&keywords=step+drill

Once your holes are done, make sure you blow out all the CF dust as it's conductive and might short something in the electronics.

Also, once the hole is made, you'll have carbon splints around the holes. Simply take a small file and file the inside and outside of the hole gently. All the splinters will come off. 

Cheers, 
A
```

---

Fancy tape removal instructions:

1. Throw the boxcutter asides,you don't need it
2. Hold box over steaming kettle until arms start to fall off or tape does
3. Peel loosely adhered tape off box slowly
4. Place in frame of your choice

## \#287 Posted by: Ovi Posted at: 2018-05-24T03:50:09.110Z Reads: 361

```
Guys just go for the complete, itâ€™s still on special and itâ€™s the dreaaaaammmm! Almost two weeks (and around 140km ) riding it and mannnn it just glides like a little cloud, I canâ€™t get enough of it and when you push that throttle it raises the little hairs on your back, it becomes thunderstruck! 

I imagine even if you want to customize it, itâ€™s easier to get the complete with the battery and all and just change the wheels/trucks as you wish although once you try it you wonâ€™t want to change a thing ! 

Everybody that tried my board loved it. One of the guys in Montreal tried it and the same day he sold his carbon GTX. I know the GTX is nothing compared to some diy boards here on the forum but again, the DSS60 is a cloud. 

I just today reached 47.1km/h on it and you really have to look at the phone to realize that you are going THAT fast. You definitely feel the kick if you hammer the throttle but in my case I had a very wide street with no cars, freshly paved, so I just slowly built up to it, the board is so stable I had no idea I was going so fast, my top speed usually hovers around 40km/h at most. The only giveaway and the reason I let go of the throttle after that was because the tires start wobbling a little at that speed (still no wobbling form the trucks!) Maybe some balancing beads would help. 

I love the idea of DIY, I donâ€™t own many objects which are not crafted or heavily customized by me but I have great trouble seeing what more you would want to pull out of the board. I mean itâ€™s just a matter of time before I lay down some custom artwork on it and design my own lights, but after two weeks on the MBS Matrix II pros I wouldnâ€™t go back to anything else and I feel bad for everybody running Trampa trucks. The battery is solid, focboxes run smooth. Iâ€™ve grown fond of the wheel design and I definitely wouldnâ€™t want to run anything heavier, especially spinning weight. I had to change a belt due to the pitiful roads we have over here in spring, I had some rocks that got stuck in it and pierced it. It took me a while to notice it as it didnâ€™t rip compeltely. I have to say itâ€™s awesome the pulleys are all metal, other than the paint getting scraped off it, the teeth look intact. And it came with two spare belts, so that was an easy fix. 

Bottom line, if youâ€™re not riding a DSS60 this summer, you are missing out. I have to admit it cost wayyyyy more than I was planning to spend. But I can confidently say itâ€™s an expensive therapy that pays off in a big way, I think you would be missing out more on the experience of riding this than on two months worth of rent money. Itâ€™s not even about the sheer power most people are looking for in a board, itâ€™s everything about it. I havenâ€™t drove a Porsche myself to compare it to it, but I can tell you it gives me the same dumb smile as driving a WRX through Vermontâ€™s winding forest roads. You are just glued to the road and you want to push it left and right, you donâ€™t even care how fast youâ€™re going, youâ€™re smiling all the way. 

Okay Iâ€™m done :) cheers guys!
```

## \#332 Posted by: Ovi Posted at: 2018-05-29T14:16:28.078Z Reads: 348

```
@philvanzu -  I thought of the same thing, and had the same worries. The spray on grip never lasts too long and isn't as grippy either. I wouldn't want to have to sand down the carbon fibre. I bought the Vicious clear tape finally after trying the cheaper Jessup. 

It's not as clear as the Jessup and definitely not as clear as the spray on option, but it definitely is grippy! I killed two scissors cutting this up. I wouldn't cover the whole board with it but I think it doesn't look half bad. Would definetly love to be able to use a laser cutter for more intricate designs.

https://www.amazon.com/Vicious-Skateboard-x11-Longboards-Skateboards/dp/B077KB8PWL/ref=sr_1_1?s=sporting-goods&ie=UTF8&qid=1527603218&sr=1-1&keywords=vicious+clear

EDIT: You do have to clean clear grip tape almost after every ride if you want it to stay clear and not brown. I use a moist carpet brush and dish soap to get the dirt out and sponge it dry with a dry rag after. On the photo above, I had just applied it, it isn't quite as clean now

![Lacroix|324x500](upload://nS5FKgOXP3ASfUkVJUHYvOMAKKF.jpg)
```

## \#345 Posted by: ervinelin Posted at: 2018-05-30T17:36:57.053Z Reads: 336

```
Can I know how you cut the hexagons so neatly? And how is it they don't shift around after time?
```

---
## \#346 Posted by: Ovi Posted at: 2018-05-30T17:52:22.660Z Reads: 360

```
hahaha motivation and patience my friend! I did that the first night I got the board actually somewhere around 2-3am. I have been waiting for about a month to get it and was experimenting with different layouts on a mockup photo and some photoshop. I tried stripes, random blobs, arrows, abunch of stuff until I came back to hexagons. 

- I printed a few different sizes and cut them off to see which size i'd prefer. 
- I then reprinted the ones I liked, I used a blade to cut it out neatly and used the negative shape to draw the hexagons on the back of the griptape sheet. 
- I took some scissors and carefully started cutting the griptape, redrawing other ones as I needed. I went through two pairs of cheap scissors.
- As I was cutting them I was just laying them on the board without sticking anything. 
- When I figured I had enough and covered the main areas, I went back to photoshop and arranged 3 hexagons next to eachother, I printed and adjusted different times until I had the distance I wanted in between them. 
- On my sheet of paper that had the 3 hexagons at the right distance in between, I then put 4-5 layers of scotch tape to make it a little more rigid and I carefully, very carefully cut out with a blade the 3 point "star" that separates the hexagons. 
- I then used that as template to lay the hexagons at almost perfect distance appart. It's a big almost, I am very perfectionist by nature, I had to make peace with my almost perfect cut hexagons and then my almost perfect cut template and ultimately my almost perfect layout - The almost increases exponentially as you go down the line :D I really wish I had access to a laser cutter.
- For the stickiness of it, I guess the vicious tape really sticks well, and also the shapes are fairly big, the board is almost 11" wide so there's a lot of sticky surface under each shape. Also helps to start with a clean smooth board.
- One thing that is useful with these patterns is to start from the middle. I started with my middle hexagon, measured and marked the middle of the deck and built around it. 

These are some of the mockups I was playing with in the beginning, I was working on a Japanese themed board, still in progress, maybe for some more rainy days, as I can't seem to get off it for more than what the charging time takes.

 ![11 AM|194x500](upload://XEjpWhW5fzUInuC6rMK5P2Idr9.jpg)![51 AM|370x500](upload://da4aYbZyVMo1nYkYmgidYCKYj3g.jpg)
```

---

And yes... I destroyed my scissors cutting vicious griptape too... Might end up just doing something much simpler for mine...
```

Mbs matrix 2 feel much more like regular skateboard trucks. They also allow more customisation, their shock block system comes with soft medium and hard blocks and each can be further compressed if you want more stability (but bigger turning circle). I feel the mbs is a better choice if you donâ€™t plan to do extreme off road riding.

## \#376 Posted by: benjammin Posted at: 2018-06-01T15:14:02.061Z Reads: 331

```
I don't have my Trampa trucks anymore so I can't say for sure, but I'm pretty sure the inner hole position of the Trampa baseplate lines up with MatrixII. 

![image|690x482](upload://vlMv9IhaMkNOLj6QYG8nRH766vm.jpeg) 

So if you're pre drilled for MatrixII, you should be able to use Trampa, but not the other way around. DK about the minis though.

Edit: might be better to drill yourself though. It'd be a fkn nightmare if they were just slightly off.
```

## \#383 Posted by: philvanzu Posted at: 2018-06-07T23:59:03.208Z Reads: 313

```
There's room for a 12S6P yes but with 2 focboxes (65x65x22mm iirc). It's the ESCapes' 70x77x18mm that I was worrying about - Since then I carved a piece of styrofoam to these dimensions and it looks like it's going to work - will only be sure when they are delivered though. 

I mostly went 12S because I had a 12S BMS. I was planning a trampa carver with 12S4P at first but reorganised my build around the lacroix deck and just bought 12 more cells since there was room for it.
```

## \#398 Posted by: philvanzu Posted at: 2018-06-08T20:47:42.825Z Reads: 314

```
I finally got my rear truck and modified motor mounts back from Overion (there were a few modifications with the newer series of Matrix II apparently and Yann had to adapt his mounts for it so I had to send my rear truck to him). 
So I was able to quickly assemble the board and hop onto it for the first time.
What an amazing feeling. The flex is absolutely perfect, flexy but not bouncy, absolutely fantastic level of comfort I have never felt like that on a skateboard before. I have the actual luxury of having wood under the whole length of my foot. Not even on my snowboard do I get that ! I'm so glad I dumped my trampa board right now :smile:
[img]https://i.imgur.com/zWP9C7B.jpg[/img]

@HeyMacfly, @pat_arch
Iâ€™ve ridden it officially 495km now in just a few days short of a full month. I can say I tangoâ€™ed with it properly. I took two falls (nothing too bad) rode on different terrains, high speed low speed, long rides, I still get shivers when I take it out. This weekend I am at the Montreal GrandPrix (F1) for work and I commute with it here, I definitely feel like a rockstar coming in with my carbon Pass helmet and the slick carbon fibre accents on the board. Everybody including security give me thumbs up as I zip through. Iâ€™m pleasantly surprised to see how easygoing cops and security have been so far. I always wave or nod first but they always respond to it. What I love about this board like I mentioned in my initial comments above is itâ€™s so unobtrusive until you floor it. People will give me strange looks when seeing my full face helmet going by ~5km/h and then zzzzzoooomm Iâ€™m gone! and I hear their exclamations fading in the back. The pneumatics have saved me so many times now itâ€™s crazy. Wear your helmet and leather/protective gloves! Cheers!

## \#440 Posted by: ervinelin Posted at: 2018-06-10T09:09:23.180Z Reads: 312

```
For anyone who's interested, I've uploaded the STLs of my LED clamp to thinigverse (https://www.thingiverse.com/thing:2954450)

![IMG20180610090306|690x388](upload://bDQNK85lYe1e3utUuvBJkXrRDKT.jpg)

There are 3 styles of adapters:
1. Slide on for front trucks (LED is centered to truck)
2. Slide on for rear trucks (LED is offset to make space for motor)
3. Clamp on for rear trucks (LED is offset to make space for motor and doesn't require you to disassemble the entire drive to install the clamp, uses 2 x M3 screws)

The LED itself just slots in sideways... should be snug enough not to dislodge itself mid ride...
```

What would be the best way to tone the acceleration down a good amount tuning the focbox's?  I've been doing some research but some of the stuff is a bit out of my comfort range.  Is the software on Enertionâ€™s site capable of doing it?  I see that people flash that userâ€™s custom firmware and tune it using that, but that seems pretty complicated and I donâ€™t really like how easy it is to mess things up.  I know itâ€™s strange but I really like boards with super mellow curves.  I tried a Trampa setup yesterday and the power was way too aggressive for me, so Iâ€™m definitely going to be interested in figuring out some way of dialing it down.

---
## \#474 Posted by: webst Posted at: 2018-06-12T15:15:24.308Z Reads: 295

```
Few options:
1. Power presets with metr.at module (you could set and change limits on the fly) - you could do the same in vesc tool (software from enertion website you mentioned) by limiting motor current
2. Ackmaniac's firmware (smoother curve)
3. Acceleration curve editor in vesc tool (I wasn't that happy with it)
4. Ride till you're comfortable
```

---
## \#475 Posted by: Adam0311 Posted at: 2018-06-12T15:22:33.491Z Reads: 291

```
i recommend trying @Ackmaniac firmware. Much smoother acceleration curve and then take it slow and get used to the board. Give it a few days/100 miles or so and if youâ€™re still not comfortable then reduce your motor current.
```

---
## \#476 Posted by: pat_arch Posted at: 2018-06-12T15:28:53.432Z Reads: 289

```
I may add that the 20T motor pulleys we use offer a smooth acceleration VS the 16T pulleys the Trampa build you tried most likely had. (we ship the boards with both pulley options)

Also, the Nano V2 remote we use comes with a ''Eco mode'' switch which limits the throttle to around 75%. When combined with the 20T pulley, this translates into a very smooth acceleration curve.
```

## \#481 Posted by: Ovi Posted at: 2018-06-12T15:57:06.455Z Reads: 302

```
@cap7ainclu7ch  - I can confirm what @pat_arch says, I run the 20T pulley. We have some roads here in Montreal that are closed to traffic for festivals and such and security makes me walk. I don't like to carry the board for a long time at 25lbs, so I switch it on "eco" mode and with a bit of practice I am able to make it roll beside me at the same speed I'm walking at with some slight nudges in between to correct direction. Somebody asked me yesterday what kind of dog is that. And yes, in the beginning I was losing balance while accelerating on the non eco mode, but a few weeks later, your body gets used to shifting the weight to keep balance.

@Adam0311 - to give you an idea, my girlfriend has a bicycle and we go riding together. She's not a pro cyclist or anything so whenever there's a steep hill I crouch on my board and grab hold of the luggage frame she has on the rear of her bike and I push her uphill with my board. We pass some of the other cyclists on the road while doing that. they all give us surprised looks because they see her all chill and not even pedalling and are expecting to see her pulling the longboard not the other way around. I was amazed how much power this board has, I can push her up some really steep hills and still feel the board accelerating. It's my arm that starts hurting after a while.
```

## \#498 Posted by: Ovi Posted at: 2018-06-13T12:22:28.398Z Reads: 311

```
Yes, it does mellow it out quite a bit. So just to clarify, the remote control has a thumb trigger that doesn't work just in two steps go or stop. You can control the amount of power your board receives by how far you push your thumb on the throttle. It does take a few minutes to get used to it but it's not a big challenge. In ECO mode everything is limited. @pat_arch could tell you probably to which amount exactly, but it does mellow out the board quite a bit. So much that I am able with careful throttle control to make it roll at walking speed beside me with no weight on it. My girlfriend when she first tried it out she was going not much faster than walking speed on it. Push that throttle down, and even on ECO mode you will find yourself zooming by at 40km/h albeit with a slower acceleration. But you will see, you won't stay for long on the eco mode. The board is very wide and stable, the learning curve is also mellow :smiley: .Also on ECO mode you might get stuck in grass or on slopes, the torque is limited. 

And to answer your question, the awesome guys from LaCroix lent me a Trampa 12sp4 board they had built last year while I was waiting for mine (we live in the same city) and that board was programmed in BLDC, so everything was a little rough, acceleration, stopping, turning on the trampa trucks was horrible if you ask me compared to the MBS. But a week later, I had gotten somewhat used to it. And I also tried for a few minutes an Evolve bamboo GTX carbon. The GTX had a somewhat destabilizing acceleration for the first few meters and it mellowed out right after. Going back on the DSS60 felt like home. I wouldn't worry too much, just keep in mind everything takes a little practice no matter what you're doing. And wear the helmet! even if your just going over to the neighbour next door.
```

---

## \#502 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-06-13T14:10:17.427Z Reads: 290

```
And just to add to this, it's one of the reasons we provide a spare wheel with pulley. So you can actually ride on the tires until one pops (from experience, your toe-side rear wheel will pop first, it takes the most beating when you carve like you're Travis Rice) and change it on the fly. It's also why we sell the tires at cost price, so you can ride without caring.
```

## \#505 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-06-13T18:06:55.995Z Reads: 294

```
Honestly, there is still a lot of life left in those tires. The initial thread goes away quite quickly, in the first 50-75km or so. After that, you can do another 400km+ on the tires being Â«slicksÂ» (i.e. sans thread, like in the picture). In fact, until you see the textile layer, you shouldn't worry about it. Just be wary if you ride on rocks because the tire is obviously thinner the more you go - but gravel has never been a problem for me, even on almost finished tires where I saw the textile in multiple spots.
```

## \#517 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-06-14T14:54:13.484Z Reads: 299

```
Erv, I believe you have red blocks in the rear - I found those to be a little to stiff. And if you ordered some orange ones and are waiting for them, in the meantime you can simply drill a small hole through them. Just pass a small drill bit through the hole underneath the Shockblock and drill straight through. You'll remove enough material to make the red block less stiff. Just FYI if ever this can help.
```

## \#524 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-06-14T15:08:51.546Z Reads: 303

```
195lbs riding weight. But i like them soft because I love to carve the living hell out of them (video coming soon). My brother, on the other hand, likes them a bit stiffer because he likes to go fast (30kmh+ in average). For me, i like to stay between 25kmh and 35kmh so I slightly compress heel side blocks, but not much. I like a soft set up. Keep in mind this board gets a little time to get used to. It really is like nothing else out there. Just take it slow. In a couple of days, you'll be ripping.
```

---
## \#525 Posted by: ervinelin Posted at: 2018-06-14T15:16:20.551Z Reads: 284

```
I agree it's totally different from my two other esk8s... Both are rigid and it's a very weird feeling to have the deck flex under my feet ...
```

---
## \#526 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-06-14T15:17:17.761Z Reads: 287

```
Exactly. The best way we found to describe it is it's a summer snowboard. That flex will actually allow you to do longer rides without fatigue, will allow you to go over potholes and curbs without even thinking about it but most importantly, will flex during heavy carving much like a snowboard in deep powder. And that's really how and where the board shines imho. Anyhow, that's just my own personal experience, I can't wait for you guys to share yours as you become more comfortable on it.
```

## \#531 Posted by: ervinelin Posted at: 2018-06-14T15:39:44.339Z Reads: 300

```
Ah! So my latching push switch has a little LED inside but that meant I needed to wire something from the back to the front of the board... 

So I just used an old 5V colour selectable LED strip that I had left over from my RC quad days, wired it to the spare 5V out from the slave VESC.

Matek RGB LED Board 5050 5V for RC Drone FPV Racing
https://banggood.app.link/urHh0ZJhKN

I removed the dip switch and hard wired it for red.

I then drilled 3 small holes and used clear hotglue to simulatenously seal the holes and hold the LED strip in place 

The only thing it does is to let me know when the board is on, nothing else... 3 dots just cos the strip has 3 LEDs... Figured it would look pretty cool.
```

## \#534 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-06-14T15:52:00.290Z Reads: 281

```
Yes, all the boards we ship come with yellows in front and orange in back. Unless you're really light, like 100-150lbs, then we'd put yellows in the back as well. 

I think if you are between 150 lbs and 250lbs riding weight, yellow in front and orange in the back allow enough adustability for just about anyone.
```

## \#552 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-06-16T03:28:47.992Z Reads: 297

```
Never be afraid to damage the battery. The board is configured with a soft cut-off to preserve the battery. Before getting into critical low voltage, we reduce the board's power substantially. When you hit that, the board will have like 30% of its power. That means you have 1-2 miles left before the board dies. And even then, when the board is "dead", it's still at a safe voltage so as to not damage the battery. 

TAKEAWAY: ride till it dies. Don't worry about the pack. We did that for you.
```

---
## \#585 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-06-21T16:00:57.574Z Reads: 322

```
Hey @philvanzu, that sucks. Most likely a bad apple. I've screwed more than 1000 now and didn't snap any. 

In my opinion, if I were to torque a screw that much to a point where it would snap, I think something else would fail first (the insert maybe? don't know). Also, as a general comment, you should not torque the screws too much. The screw should go in easy and when you start feeling resistance when the nylon washer (underneath the countersunk washer) is touching the enclosure, maybe do one revolution (or less), then stop. 

The screws are M3 phillips because as you can see, they sit just a fraction of a millimiter under the countersunk washer. This enables the washer to be on a very slight angle on the sections of the deck that are curved. As the holes for the inserts in the deck are made with a 3 axis CNC and not a 5 axis CNC, the holes are not always at 90 degrees with the top of the deck - sometimes at 88 or 89 degrees. So the M3 screw being just below the countersunk washer allows this washer to move a slight bit and compensate for that 1 degree or 2 degree. 

I know this is some solid geekery but all this to say that if you choose to get other screws, perhaps screws that sit perfectly in the washer (and that doesn't allow for this 1 or 2 degree movement), then maybe some of the screws will not sit perfectly flat on the enclosure. Also, we wanted all the screws to be all black (because aesthetics ;) So that is the reason we used these specific countersunk Philipps M3 screws.

But by all means, if you do find another solution (other screws that would do), please share. This is one of the reasons why we offered the deck+enclosure at the community, to get your feedback and ideas and implement them.

Also, for those wondering, we used M3 and not M4 to keep the hole in the enclosure as small as possible as to maintain its integrity and strenght as much as we could. And after looking at the spec numbers, M3 could more than handle the weight so we went in that direction.

As for replacement, I should have sent you a couple extras right? Let me know if not and I'll send you a couple in the mail.
```

---
## \#586 Posted by: philvanzu Posted at: 2018-06-21T17:51:13.660Z Reads: 303

```

## \#616 Posted by: banjaxxed Posted at: 2018-06-27T09:49:09.886Z Reads: 295

```
Probably Sanyo NCR20700B 4250mAh - 15A ? interesting. but for the price difference it's not really worth it, you need to almost double-down on cell costs.

Tries some calcs...open to correction, weight difference fairly negligible

60 30Q in 10s6p = 90A+ discharge, capacity 18Ah, 666Wh @ nominal 3.7v cell voltage
Pack weight: 2880g

50 NCR20700B in 10s5p = 75A+ discharge, capacity 21.25Ah, 786.25Wh @ nominal 3.7v cell voltage
Pack weight = 3150g

I don't know how much of a badass the NCR20700B  is for discharge, maybe in real life a 5p can take on a 30Q 6p for discharge.

Personally I'd prefer to get a spare 40 30Q cells for another build at the same cost...
```

---
## \#617 Posted by: deucesdown Posted at: 2018-06-27T14:55:44.178Z Reads: 275

```
There's one more angle for cost comparison -- cycle life. I think 30q are 250-300 cycles to 70%. 20700B looks like about 500 cycles at similar discharge rates. So that makes up the price gap.

But I'm with you, unless prices come down by a lot, 30q is king.
```

---

## \#623 Posted by: slybarman Posted at: 2018-06-27T17:50:35.091Z Reads: 273

```
I would be interested if anyone can comment on this board's suspension. I see it does not have springs, how well does it handle uneven pavement, etc. 

I am torn between a fully built board like the DSS60 and building my own board like a Trampa Urban Carve.
```

---
## \#624 Posted by: Ovi Posted at: 2018-06-27T18:05:45.105Z Reads: 282

```
@slybarman  Hi, if you're looking for spring suspension, you would need a Bajaboard. Both the springs and bushings in the trucks of the Trampa vs the DSS60 only fulfill the function of steering dampening. The board itself absorbs shocks and vibrations but not the trucks directly. And from that point of view both the Trampa and the DSS60 are flexible decks. The hump on the Trampa is a foot killer in my experience, horrible cramps from the shape of the deck and no concave means you never know where your feet are on the board. In my own experience the Trampa doesn't even come close in any way (Not an endorsed advertisement). However if you're planning on off-roading, maybe there's room for discussion. The beautiful carbon fibre case of the DSS60 is heart breaking to scratch on rocks, and it is closer to the ground than the Trampa board I used. You could always use 8" knobbed tires on the DSS60, but again, I feel it shines at its brightest on pavement, like a Porsche ;)
```

## \#642 Posted by: Blasto Posted at: 2018-06-28T15:56:56.139Z Reads: 293

```
1: hold for 5 to 10 secs for reverse throttle (up becomes brake, down accel) resets on power cycle

2: hold to toggles 0-5V on channel 2 of receiver

![image|511x500](upload://jp49rl3ylPLwJ6nSW1gvNrVaaav.jpeg)
```

## \#663 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-07-01T02:56:57.697Z Reads: 280

```
I believe you have MBS 8 inch tires right? Anyhow, we don't use them on ur completes but specially for the rear wheels, you need to be super careful on the pulley placement because if it's 0.5mm out of true then it will cause wobble. We 3D printed a little jig to center the pulley on the hub before tightening the screws and we are going to upload the file to the website in a couple of days so everyone can just 3D print their own little centering jig. When I use it, I hardly feel anything, no wobble at all. Also, if you must, balancing beads work well too; https://www.amazon.ca/DIYK-4-Counteract-Tire-Balancing-Beads/dp/B06W2N5MTW/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1530413895&sr=8-1&keywords=balancing+beads

Our tires are rated 36psi but I inflate them at 50psi without any issues.
```

---
## \#664 Posted by: ervinelin Posted at: 2018-07-01T03:08:02.699Z Reads: 276

```
I am using MBS tires and hubs, without the pulley it wobbles already even without power.
```

## \#671 Posted by: HeyMacfly Posted at: 2018-07-02T00:20:52.124Z Reads: 268

## \#672 Posted by: Ovi Posted at: 2018-07-02T01:39:00.294Z Reads: 275

```
I don't have a scale so I used the valve caps as measure. I first added 2 and then added another one. Its a little tricky. If you don't add enough it won't solve your problem and if you add too much it can get worse, especially at low speeds. You can feel the vibration almost instantly disappear after 25km/h it's strange it's like a switch going off. For the beads to even out it takes some centrifugal force, and I noticed under 25km/h not much happens and especially if you have too many beads at slower speed they tend to stay all in one spot and worsen wobble. I advise you start with a little bit, ride for a few days and add more if needed after. Also, YOU WILL MAKE A MESS. Make yourself a funnel out of paper if you don't have one that small to fit in the valve already and add a few beads at a time. It helps if you gently tap the valve end as your pour them down. Hope this helps!
```

## \#677 Posted by: HeyMacfly Posted at: 2018-07-05T12:13:18.493Z Reads: 282

```
I read a review about Nano V2 remote and there is something that worries me. 
https://www.electric-skateboard.builders/t/nano-v2-full-review/25159

"BIGGEST con to this remote is the auto-bind feature. Aside from possibly taking a long time to bind (anywhere from 1-10 seconds, usually faster though) it does not remember PPM positions across reboots of the remote. Once you turn it off and on you have to throttle all the way back and all the way forward after the remote binds in order for it to know min/max PPM. If you donâ€™t do this, the SLIGHTEST change in PPM signal will give you either max acceleration or max braking. This nearly made me fly off my board the first couple times until I figured out what was wrong."

There is a interview with Alex from Lacroix boards >
https://graeme-franks.squarespace.com/lacroixboards-faq

"3) Reading the review of the remote, they say you need to calibrate it every time because it doesnâ€™t remember â€œMin or Max speedâ€ is this what you do? And how do you do it?

Once you turn on the remote, you throttle to the max and brake to the max. Then you turn on the board, the remote will bind and that's it. So it's just doing max throttle and max brake when you turn on the remote. "
```

## \#709 Posted by: banjaxxed Posted at: 2018-07-09T14:29:30.275Z Reads: 273

```
My feelings are that a 9" or 10" option for real offroad makes a lot of sense for not too much extra weight.
**9" tire option:** 2.80/2.50 - 4
So you get an exra 15mm in width too, this spreads load and helps stop spinning wheel problems. For me it's primarily dealing with sand, at present I can't even go near anything not hard-packed, but muddy backroads, green lane trails, probably a similar problem

Caveat: I have not tries 8" Trampa mud pluggers yet.

The power would be plenty from a dual 6374 even from a standstill & top speed only increases which is maybe a danger if anything, downside? Maybe a little extra weight but it's largely insignificant on the type of build under discusssion.

You can already do a chain or pulley driven 9" build using Trampa, MBS or DIY printed hubs, I am hoping for a vendor produced hub/wheel drive combo, I don't want to say anything and step on any vendor announcement

But watch this space and save your shekels for concentrated off-road awesomeness
```

---
## \#712 Posted by: TarzanHBK Posted at: 2018-07-09T15:08:13.428Z Reads: 242

```
there are a few 7 inch offroad wheels available from MBS, I also think that all standard 8 inch wheels fit aswell without modification @Arch?
```

---
## \#713 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-07-09T15:15:47.953Z Reads: 256

```
Yep, they fit 7 inch as well. As long as the hub is 3.75 inch in diameter, it will fit all known 7inch and 8 inch AT tires. In fact, the Rockstar2 might not fit MBS's 7 inch tire (which they only sell on a 3 spoke hub), but it will fit Innova 7 inch tires and Evolve tires as well. So when MBS says it will only fit 8 inch tires (and not 7 inch tires), they only refer to their own 7 inch tires, not 7 inch tires in general. It's confusing, I'll give you that.
```

---
## \#714 Posted by: banjaxxed Posted at: 2018-07-09T15:22:28.927Z Reads: 275

```
For 9" you need to use the Fivestar hubs, whether they have the same hole pattern as Rockstar II, not sure.

They do have an extra lip inside to handle fitment of both 8" and 9" tires
![image|690x250](upload://8utD3NtO2U4WF8vWMnLFITl6xKt.jpg)
![image|690x256](upload://pxQ4o6yRxWDb3XzVF5H4nXvEMC6.jpg)
```

## \#740 Posted by: webst Posted at: 2018-07-12T23:27:06.779Z Reads: 252

```
[quote="JohnnyMeduse, post:738, topic:49051"]
How Many Amp are you talking about ?
[/quote]
8A for 10S4P 30Q setup at 0,6C rate, where 0,5 is standard charge for 30Q and 1,3C is fast charge. Safe for batteries but charger will be pretty bulky. Iâ€™m charging 10S2P LiPos with 4A, starting from 37V in 1,5h which gives around 6Ah that allows me to ride for 20km with average speed of 20kmh (going up to 50). I could always go with lower cuttoff voltage but why bother when itâ€™s full relatively fast.
```

---
## \#741 Posted by: JohnnyMeduse Posted at: 2018-07-13T02:15:52.976Z Reads: 254

```
Actually after I won't really recommend to go over the 4A charger that come with the board, not that the battery won't take it, but some component inside are not conceive with a different charger in mind. Switching the charger for a bigger one comme at your own risk.
```

---
## \#742 Posted by: webst Posted at: 2018-07-13T07:49:47.903Z Reads: 251

```
Still: 2,5 - 4,5h charge is acceptable, I've seen some Chinese brands that needed 6h charge and went 15km afterwards.
```

We really hope that you are recovering from your accident and feeling better.

## \#803 Posted by: Grozniy Posted at: 2018-07-20T17:21:28.994Z Reads: 223

```

```

---
## \#804 Posted by: nw-esk8 Posted at: 2018-07-20T18:05:58.807Z Reads: 244

```
Yes, the Sanyo's have a much better cycle rating, but 30q's are the best (that I've seen) w/r/t the amount lost per their cycle rating among the top 18650 cells... I think they lose 6% over their rated cycle life (most others I've seen are closer to 10%).  The other thing to consider is how you are planning on using your board.  IE: if you only charge to 80-90% and don't discharge it below 20%, then you should be able to extend the cycle life on the 30qs into the thousands as well.  If you're charging to full and running it into the ground (as the other extreme), then the cycle life is going to be a bigger factor.

In my experience (_mostly_ from ebikes), the best way to keep a balanced pack happy and healthy is to keep it between 20%-85% and then once every 20-30 cycles, charge to full and let the BMS balance the cells (otherwise, if you never charge to 100% the voltages between packs can get out of whack).

Personally, I opted for the DSS50+.  Between the cycle rating and how the cells discharge, the Sanyos were a better fit for me, because I wanted to maximize the range while keeping the cells from spending too much time below 3.2v (SAnyos drop off pretty hard after 3.2v where the Samsung drop is more gradual, meaning more of the total capacity is in the usable range for Sanyo's (lacroix has soft cutoff at 3.2v, IIRC)).  

Based on the cutoff limits and some isolated test results, it appears that the Sanyo pack may only have ~11% more range total (down to the 2.9v hard cutoff... which is purely based on Mooch's testing, which rated the Sanyo cells at 16a ~4000mah vs the commonly advertised 15a 4250mah) than the Samsung pack (if ridden to the board's 2.9v cutoff), but the Sanyo pack has 25% more range before hitting the 3.2v soft cutoff, which was significant for me, since that's level I want to stay above, unless forced otherwise.  This also assumes a 'coasting' load of ~15A draw from the battery... a spike in current when running low would cause voltage drops which could trigger the cutoffs sooner, etc (not sure how the 6p of Samsungs handles voltage sag compared to the 5p Sanyos, so that's not taken into consideration).

^ kind of a lot of random thoughts combined with limited testing/rating results + dirty analysis, etc, but maybe that helped answer your question? :sweat_smile:
```

---
## \#805 Posted by: Ovi Posted at: 2018-07-20T18:47:00.945Z Reads: 236

```
I have around 1150km on my DSS60 so far and I haven't been too cautious with battery charging, most of the time charging it to 95%, and discharging it to ~ 20%  most of the time but I have been discharging to lower than that a few times lately as I've gotten a lot more comfortable riding it the past weeks. I crave to go further and accelerate harder and climb steeper hills. So far my top range since I have the board was 42km on a full charge, at the end I had 2% left. The last 2 km were mostly assisted pushing so I'm not sure if that counts. I weigh ~73-75KG depending on my lunch. Nowadays I ride about 30-35km on a good day and use ~80-85% of the battery doing that. But there are quite a few hills I go up where I live. And for the regenerative braking, in my experience there's not much going back into the batteries, maybe the BMS is too restrictive or maybe I don't brake enough :D 

We would need to have graphene ultra capacitors in our boards :D https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KQ2Eo6wl5r0

I will keep you updated on how my battery keeps up with time, from what I understand the price of a new battery is a massive hit to the wallet, I hope I can comfortably stretch it over the next summer as well, but I definitely crave more range already. If my board could do it, I would go on camping trips with this thing. I would love to get 70-80km range out of it in fun mode.
```

We are doing a second one with Surf Rodz TKPs (adjustable base plates).  I think I can fit @psychotiller sixshooters in this config.  But my buddy pushed around and road some hills with some 107s, and he wants that instead.

Hell, I don't blame him. It carves and rides like a dream.  Seriously just insane.  I can't wait to share the build process with everybody soon.

@mmaner pushed it around analog style, and I think he would agree that this setup will be next level!!!

Also, as an aside, It gets me so psyched that you guys are leaving careers to focus on this BADASSERY!  So fucking cool. I am very happy for you! @pat_arch @Arch. Literally gives me more chills! LOL #sojelly
```

## \#846 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-07-21T20:09:45.026Z Reads: 237

```
The situation with the board in NYC is simple. The board had a FOCBOX behaving weirdly (it happens sometimes. One in about 100 I'd say. And when they fail, they fail fast, i.e. in the first few weeks). So we sent a new one and it was replaced. However, with the new FOCBOXes, the board (against our recommendations) was ridden with only a few screws supporting the enclosure. (To be clear, all screws should always be there. If one is loose, take it off, put Permatex blue gel on it and screw it back on. Never ride with anything less than 100% of the screws on at all time. No exceptions). And Max had back luck to boot. While riding the board with the enclosure only hanging with a handful of screws, he rode in a patch of diesel (or other solvent, we can't be sure). So the board was in quarantine for a little while. However, if you follow Max's stories on IG, you can see him riding his DSS50+ so everything worked out in the end ;-)
```

## \#881 Posted by: Ovi Posted at: 2018-07-24T02:08:55.530Z Reads: 241

```
Yeah I love everything about the blade runner aesthetic. My end goal for the board is to have it look like a colourful Japanese toy but without going overboard on the details, keeping the design somewhat minimal. I have a deep appreciation of the obsessive Japanese craftsmanship whether it is woodworking or pottery, or anything creative there are people that dedicate a huge amount of time to details and I thought it wasnâ€™t too far off from what the DSS60 stands for. And yeah the grip... It got dirty beyond cleaning. I still try to clean it after every ride but some of the dirt baked into it. But youâ€™re right it gives it character. It does have 1200KMon it after all
```

---
## \#882 Posted by: Ovi Posted at: 2018-07-24T02:12:07.847Z Reads: 241

```
The board comes with a 5th whole wheel actually and bearings so you can simply swap it out if ever you roll on something too sharp. I had one flat so far around 500km, I rolled onto an industrial staple that pierced the tire. Otherwise so far glass didnâ€™t get through and neither did the other tons of sharp debris on our dirty streets. A set of tires lasts at least 600km with heavy riding. And they sell a setof tires and tubes for 35$. I suggest you take out the board for a few KM before getting extra tires, if youâ€™re not carving too hard you can get more than 600km.
```

## \#893 Posted by: DWU Posted at: 2018-07-25T17:55:55.666Z Reads: 221

```
How do you guys carry the board without a bag? Does it hold comfortably with a one arm side carry? Can you drag it on the ground like a luggage?
```

---
## \#894 Posted by: Ovi Posted at: 2018-07-25T18:24:10.369Z Reads: 224

```
unfortunately, with the standard motor mounts you cannot drag it by the front trucks. I spoke with @Arch and he said when they designed the motor mounts they thought about the possibility of the board flipping upside down during a crash and wanted to protect the motors. This brings them too low to drag it by the front trucks. I drag it by holding the motor can. It can be carried like a snowboard on your side but at 25lbs you need the arms that go with it. I'm not a fan of attaching it to my backpack so I try to be on it most of the time even if it means taking a detour
```

---
## \#895 Posted by: HeyMacfly Posted at: 2018-07-25T18:29:09.390Z Reads: 217

Not a problem if you work out a lot. :)
```

## \#919 Posted by: Ovi Posted at: 2018-07-28T16:38:58.444Z Reads: 242

```
I got a â€œunder voltage faultâ€ as my board shut down and the efficiency meter cleared up. But it saved in the runs summary. 8.7 for one motor. 

![image|281x500](upload://sXkBotEw1PDuQXgxrKrwn3K8MNX.jpeg)

EDIT: worth mentioning, I had changed belts before this run, the old ones became pretty loose, and the new ones feel a lot tighter, so I imagine more friction. Add to that a heavy backpack, slopes, high wind gusts and just massive sprints, I think I cruised at 45-48/h for a good km or two.
```

---
## \#920 Posted by: Ovi Posted at: 2018-07-28T17:00:53.027Z Reads: 227

```
I used to run 50 ish. Now I go much lower, it wasn't very comfortable and I hadn't noticed a significant range improvement, a lot of the momentum was wasted by the vibrations. I now run 40 but i haven't checked the tires in a few hundred kms, they could be a tad below 40. It's definitely more comfortable than running 50 psi and the tires stay more round and vibrate less
```

---
## \#921 Posted by: HeyMacfly Posted at: 2018-07-28T17:03:04.406Z Reads: 224

```
Less psi = Less range and speed.
```

---
## \#922 Posted by: Ovi Posted at: 2018-07-28T17:14:01.361Z Reads: 235

```
I regret not having the Sanyo. I bought my board in the first week the company was launched, I didn't even get that option, granted I probably wouldn't have went for it at that time since this is my first eboard. The advertised capacity with the 30q's seemed already overkill at first. I did already get a 42km ride on my current setup but after 1200+ kms I'm getting quite a bit more comfortable with the board and I feel that I control it more than it controls me so I go a bit faster and carve a little harder and I got used to break full force when I need to, my wheels lock up when I break. So there's a lot more stress on the battery. But also depends on where you live. I live on the suburbs of Montreal, so just crossing in the city is 11km, back and forth is 22, which leaves me about 10km of available range to spend in the city. If your commute is shorter you won't use the full battery. 

@Arch even with 1300km, if we calculate an average of 35km per full cycle, that leaves me at only 37ish full charge cycles. But that is the worst case scenario, because not all my rides used a full cycle. Aren't the 30q's rated for 200 cycles before battery reaches 70% capacity ?
```

## \#926 Posted by: Ovi Posted at: 2018-07-28T19:52:28.781Z Reads: 221

```
Yes battery life can be substantially increased if you use a shorter discharge-recharge range. The charger only takes it to 41.7 ish and board shuts off at 29V (soft cutoff at 32V). So itâ€™s already protected against any major damage and itâ€™s a shame to limit your trips on a 60cell battery pack just to try to prolong its battery life (opinion).
```

## \#957 Posted by: Photorph Posted at: 2018-08-02T05:45:31.151Z Reads: 233

```
TSG pass does look cool.  But I looked at the following things in a full face helmet.

-Certifications
-ventilation
-comfort
-MIPS

The helmet best suited for esk8 are helmets like the bell super DH or the fox pro frame, or at least that's the conclusion I came to after spending a lot of time researching and trying out helmets.  They have much better ventilation than TSG pass, they are lighter, they are more protective and have more certifications, and they have MIPS.  Another huge benefit over the TSG pass is that the strap is magnetic, the D rings on the TSG pass are a pain to take on/off.  

I went from predator DH6 full face (similar to TSG pass), S1 helmet, and now for my lacroix I'll be getting a downhill MTB helmet like the one I mentioned above.  

This guy also has a bell mtb helmet.  They may not look as cools as a TSG pass or a ruroc, but you'll wear them actually and they are more functional.

https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DHZoOKA1w2Y
```

## \#965 Posted by: cap7ainclu7ch Posted at: 2018-08-02T07:33:38.872Z Reads: 213

```
I love my Super DH.  Will be my primary helmet for riding my LaCroix.  Light mounted on the GoPro mount is super easy to remove for charging. Coverts easily to open face for hot days.  Plenty of ventilation.  Dual EPS/EPP layered for low/high speed impacts, along with Bell's custom "mk2" MIPS system (cerified for DH which is a pretty intense certification).  Also happens to be comfortable and has a sweet magnetic buckle.  It's a badass helmet.

Also just got my board.  Thing is a beast.  Super easy to control.  However the rear end feels a bit loose for my taste.  I tried tightening up the blocks, but still carves a little too hard at speed for me.  Should I consider swapping out for the red's?  I like having to really throw my weight into the carve and generally run the front of my boards loose and the rears stiff.  Stock for me just feels a bit squirrelly during turning at speed.  

Otherwise everything is perfect.  So much fun being able to fly over roads I know I'd be crawling on with my crappy hub-motor board.  Really does feel like a cloud.  Can't wait to get the trucks dialed in for me.
```

## \#969 Posted by: cap7ainclu7ch Posted at: 2018-08-04T08:45:31.656Z Reads: 210

```
Okay after a few more rides and some tweaking I can safely say that this is probably the best purchase I've ever made.  Pretty much everything I've ever wanted for street riding.  Comfortable, controllable, stupid fast, and just overall awesome.  I know its been said many times already in this thread, but if you are on the fence about getting one of these, just do it.  

This thing does the slow cruise just as well as it does a decent impression of a ballistic missile.  Kind of reminds me of a hypercar like the Chiron in that way.  It's a nice feeling knowing that while you are just putting along you have WAY too much power on tap if you want it.  

As for the trucks I've just been experimenting with different tightnesses and have slowly been figuring out what I like.  As I mentioned earlier I prefer a stiffer setup so during high speeds I can still shift my weight around.  I don't like feeling like I have to be super careful like you do when you run them loose.  I know it sacrifices slow speed maneuverability but thats just preference.

I will say the only problem I have so far is in regarding to slow speed braking.  The board brakes flawlessly but once it gets to around 3-5mph the board just locks it up and jolts you.  Nothing more embarrassing than flying up to a light with full gear on with a badass board like this and then almost eating it at walking speed.  Is there something wrong with my FOCBOX setup or is this just normal behavior?  I just started braking early and then rolling to a stop instead.  This is really my only true complaint with the board. 

Also how do I go about connecting to the board via bluetooth.  Do I need to open it up in order to pair it to my phone?

Anyways great job guys and keep up the good work.  You've made a hell of a first product.
```

---
## \#970 Posted by: ervinelin Posted at: 2018-08-04T09:07:05.730Z Reads: 202

```
The jolt at the end seems to be a software issue running FOC on large wheels... There's a thread on this and no one could resolve it.

Current work around is to just get off the board at the very last second before the jolt kicks in.
```

---
## \#971 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-08-04T09:52:01.773Z Reads: 214

```
Glad you're enjoying the board ;-) for the Bluetooth, no need to open up the board (ever, in fact), simply download any app and go through the pairing process in the app. That's all that needs to be done.

As for wheels locking up at 1mph, as @ervinelin stated, it's a focbox quirk and nothing can be done about it. You'll learn to work around it. I do either 2 things ; slam on the brakes and shift my body weight backwards when I'm almost at a full stop to compensate the lock OR let off the throttle a second early and coast to a stop.
```

## \#1050 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-08-14T01:15:13.125Z Reads: 214

```
PSA: for those receiving their DSS50+ and DSS60 since the past week - you will notice we did not include an extra wheel with pulley, nor extra belts, nor extra pulleys. It's not that we don't love you or that we are starting to cheap out. We are simply low on parts so we prefer to stretch out all the parts we have so we could ship more boards and you can ride. When we receive a couple of YUUUUUUUGE shipments before the end of August, we'll send you all a little package by the mail that will include all these little bits. On us, of course.
```

## \#1093 Posted by: gmurad Posted at: 2018-08-20T22:01:56.740Z Reads: 230

```
Here are my range stats on my first 3 rides on the 10s6p 30q Lacroix:

Weight: 225lbs + clothing, gear and backpack 

All rides started with the battery full.

First Ride: 13km, 38V (Literally went up a mountain on a gravel road, about 4km uphill)
Second Fide: 17.86km, 37.V (Doing some speed tests up to 50km/h and some riding on grass)
Third Ride: 37.5km, 29.8V (Board stopped completely)

(distance, final voltage)

Pretty much what I expected, just above the range that I need.
```

## \#1113 Posted by: gmurad Posted at: 2018-08-25T12:01:16.879Z Reads: 232

```
Are you charging the board at work before coming back? I have the same weight (225lbs) but the max range I got (riding all the way to the board stopping ~29.8V) was 36 km and I only ride on the slower remote mode. Granted I have the 30Q version but still it's 18 km difference, I'd expect a difference (real world difference) of 6 to 10 kms.

The deck length was one of my first observations as well, being 188cm the deck is just a bit short for me to get a stance wide enough that would feel 100% comfortable to handle all the power that the board has, but it's something that I compensate for by lowering my stance more then usual so not a deal breaker but i'm always trying to move my feet further apart. Overall in terms of body pain it's still the most comfortable ride I have even riding 36 kms.

Here is a picture of my 36km range test, the battery died right after I crossed a very long bridge (the one parallel to Champlain Bridge) and there were no roads for cars on the other side, so I had to carry the board back. I made a leash and halfway through I realized I can just push the board manually :laughing:

![IMG_20180820_142320|666x500](upload://sw0QEFSgSPNAf2ymnAMwHcfAfg8.jpg)
```

## \#1121 Posted by: BOOSTEDO Posted at: 2018-08-25T18:03:25.923Z Reads: 229

```
Yes Sir Indeedy... I have a Raptor2 exclusive build and it uses the same charger as LaCroix/Evolve so one charger stays at work and the other at home... I always charge up at work before I head back home - I let the board sit for an hour or so before I start the recharge for the journey home. 

 I was asking Pat and Alex for the @Maxaweli 20700B build from the moment I knew it was done. I knew from my Raptor2 experience that you had better get the most Wh possible to deal with the occasional hill popping up and taking the thrill out of your ride. The Raptor 2 can barely make the 17 mile trip home in R-Spec mode... But the Raptor2 is way more subway friendly than the Lacroix... 

I have to check my tire pressures on the Lacroix and maybe use some white lithium grease on the axles and bearings. I've noticed on Summer Fridays as I'm only at work for 3.5 hours (I don't have a full 4 hours + to let the Lacroix fully charge). I let the Lacroix sit for 1/2 hour to cool down so at most I get 3 hours of charging but no green light on the charger before I leave for home... 

Yesterday it felt as if the board went to it's lowest setting around the 15 mile point... It's a slow drag incline for a good 1/2 mile and I punched the throttle but no hyperspace! The sublight engines got me up the hill though... Once it flattened out then the speed started building again.  

On my boosted V2 I can get home (same exact route) using 2 XR(extended range) batteries with 20% left on the last XR battery... but that's on Thane... 1 XR can get me 9 miles on pretty much the flattest part of Manhattan. 1 boosted XR battery is rated at 267Wh so 534Wh in total compared to 432Wh for the Raptor2 vs 666Wh for the DSS60 vs 786 for the DSS50+...  

 I'm glad I waited for the DSS50+ now I just need a longer deck with room for a bonafide 12s5p or 12s6p inside... Oh and a faster Charger!!:wink:
@pat_arch @Arch  

Ride Safe!:pray:t6:
```

## \#1198 Posted by: Frank-Love Posted at: 2018-09-02T12:33:53.384Z Reads: 240

```
Before reassembling the tire on the wheel, put tire liners it work like magic on my bicycle. 
It protects the tube if a sharp object passes through the tire.  
There several brand, all work well. 
Take one that is wide enough to cover the contact surface of the wheel. 


https://www.amazon.ca/Slime-Bicycle-Tire-Liners-26-Inch/dp/B000ENSRQW/ref=sr_1_2?ie=UTF8&qid=1535890908&sr=8-2&keywords=mr+tuffy

https://www.amazon.ca/Tuffy-Bicycle-Liner-Orange-20-25/dp/B000C191I4/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&qid=1535890908&sr=8-1&keywords=mr+tuffy

https://www.amazon.ca/Clean-Motion-RhinoDillos-Bicycle-Liners/dp/B0066DGZ4K/ref=sr_1_3?ie=UTF8&qid=1535890908&sr=8-3&keywords=mr+tuffy
```

## \#1214 Posted by: rich Posted at: 2018-09-03T22:57:52.485Z Reads: 236

```
As @Grozniy linked, my tires were solid rubber with ultra heavy mega breaking resistance :laughing:

The tire of Aliexpress is a real tire (nylon) filled with foam. On the tire you see "inflate to 36 psi". I don't know how much the foam changes the rolling resistance but it doesn't look bad. Give it a try.

[quote="Blitqz, post:1196, topic:49051"]
got a flat on the 4th day
[/quote]

I had flats all the time and once twice a day. I was carrying 2 spare tubes and tools in my backpack. It was a PIA. Since I use tire sealant (for bicycle tubes) I had no single flat and it's great to ride without spare tubes and fear of the next flat.


![155156e|690x311](upload://iorZKdNyqffeOkghawqnQEnpNPZ.jpg)![005343e|690x245](upload://gr3C4QD35xO4hoc2qkk0GzR4lE7.jpg)

A bottle (for 2 bicycle tubes) is enough for 8x tubes. The first time I used 1 bottle for 4 tubes but that's not necessary. No flats but if the tire explodes it looks like that :laughing:

![Bang3e|690x388](upload://cLmks0VmvxIsjASd8t8thvV9Uoc.jpg)
```

## \#1222 Posted by: daj013 Posted at: 2018-09-05T22:02:07.844Z Reads: 216

```
I had a Evolve GTX with the R1 remote. That remote worked the same way, when you pulled the throttle back you would go forward. I have ordered a Psychotiller custom board as well an it uses the standard RC mini remote. The throttle function on that works the same way, pull the lever back and you go forward, push the lever forward and you apply the brakes. Since I will be using both boards, they both will function the same way and I won't have to remember that I am using a different remote.
```

---
## \#1223 Posted by: Grozniy Posted at: 2018-09-05T22:27:01.160Z Reads: 211

```
For safety reasons, it's better to pull forward to go forward. The reason being is "whisky throttle". When one falls or panicks, the natural reaction is to close the hands, in this case it could be to pull back on the lever. So if the throttle is reversed, board could fly forward :man_shrugging:
```

---
## \#1224 Posted by: Frank-Love Posted at: 2018-09-05T22:40:52.599Z Reads: 219

```
@daj013: I understood your concern. I will suggest you to modify all your boards to use the same remote. (Youâ€™re lucky you have thing to work with during winter time)  

@Grozniy : Thanks for the â€œwhisky throttleâ€  I will remember for ever! I drink to that!
```

## \#1242 Posted by: philvanzu Posted at: 2018-09-12T22:58:16.599Z Reads: 240

```
On smooth pavement the gummies are super good, real grippy, super reactive, they give a real kick when accelerating and they drag a lot less when coasting. I kinda prefer carving on pneu though, they carve a bit more abruptly, maybe I should try tightening my shockbocks a bit more.

On bad pavement they really stressed my build though, a lot of rattling, I had to retighten everything on arrival.
They feel a lot less grippy as soon as thereâ€™s a bit of small gravel or sand on the road, or on irregular pavementâ€¦ no carving there.

I have to say though it still felt very rideable thanks to shock absorbing risers and mostly to the Lacroix deck and its flex.

Range wise I did get the same range I usually have with 6.5" at 85 PSI, though i had to battle against a strong headwind most of the way, and I did not slow down or tuck it out, just kept my snowboard stance.

I was afraid to scar my enclosure with only 1/2" risers; it's a little lower than normal but it worked, I did not hit anything, even when carving hard.
```

## \#1256 Posted by: BOOSTEDO Posted at: 2018-09-18T01:54:29.761Z Reads: 239

```
The 7" evolve wheels work... You just need to put a speed ring(spacer/washer) 12mm on the rear axel before you install the wheels... I rode the Lacroix over the Williamsburg Bridge with all those huge gaps and No Problemo... I was riding with 40 psi... if the clearance is still an issue then grab the 2mm allen key and move the motor pulleys closer to the motors (I had to do this for 1 of the wheels)... You should be good to go...:+1:t6::wink:
```

## \#1259 Posted by: Arch Posted at: 2018-09-19T03:38:28.310Z Reads: 224

```
Thanks for pointing that out. It had slipped me and we just corrected the website. On our first handful of boards, we shipped with the Pro and then MBS went out of stock on the Pros (and has been since June) so if we had waited for those, we would not have shipped any boards this summer. So we shipped our boards with the standard Matrix2 (which are 0.07lbs heavier - 31 grams to be exact - they drill a hole in the center of the axle to lighten the PRO. It's the only difference between the 2). As we don't have any, we won't be able to swap those - this said, please email me at alex@lacroixboards.com so we can discuss how to move forward and make you happy. Also, I invite any other LaCroix owner who feels the same way to do the same. Thanks and sorry again about this, it was my oversight.
```
